If there are many streams\n715:   // that may result in a stack overflow. This flag is used to avoid above recursion.\n716:   if (drained_due_to_premature_resets_) {\n717:     return;\n718:   }\n719: \n720:   if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ == 0) {\n721:     return;\n722:   }\n723: \n724:   const uint64_t limit =\n725:       runtime_.snapshot().getInteger(ConnectionManagerImpl::PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey, 500);\n726: \n727:   if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit) {\n728:     // Even though the total number of streams have not reached `limit`, check if the number of bad\n729:     // streams is high enough that even if every subsequent stream is good, the connection\n730:     // would be closed once the limit is reached, and if so close the connection now.\n731:     if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < limit) {\n732:       return;\n733:     }\n734:   } else {\n735:     if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_) {\n736:       return;\n737:     }\n738:   }\n739: \n740:   if (read_callbacks_->connection().state() == Network::Connection::State::Open) {\n741:     stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.inc();\n742: \n743:     // Mark the the connection has been drained due to too many premature resets.\n744:     drained_due_to_premature_resets_ = true;\n745: \n746:     doConnectionClose(Network::ConnectionCloseType::Abort, absl::nullopt,\n747:                       \"too_many_premature_resets\");\n748:   }\n749: }\n750: \n751: void ConnectionManagerImpl::onGoAway(GoAwayErrorCode) {\n752:   // Currently we do nothing with remote go away frames. void ConnectionManagerImpl::ActiveStream::maybeRecordLastByteReceived(bool end_stream) {\n1303:   // If recreateStream is called, the HCM rewinds state and may send more encodeData calls.\n1304:   if complicated, but important.\n1312: //\n1313: // We want to do minimal work before selecting route and creating a filter\n1314: // chain to maximize the number of requests which get custom filter behavior,\n1315: // e.g. registering access logging.\n1316: //\n1317: // This must be balanced by doing sanity checking for invalid requests (one\n1318: // can't route select properly without full headers), checking state required to\n1319: // serve error responses (connection close, head requests, etc), and\n1320: // modifications which may themselves affect route selection.\n1321: void \\n259: void ConnectionManagerImpl::doEndStream(ActiveStream& stream, bool check_for_deferred_close) {\\n260:   // The order of what happens in this routine is important and a little complicated. We first see\\n261:   // if the stream needs to be reset. If it needs to be, this will end up invoking reset callbacks\\n262:   // and then moving the stream to the deferred destruction list. If the stream has not been reset,\\n263:   // we move it to the deferred deletion list here. Then, we potentially close the connection. This\\n264:   // must be done after deleting the stream since the stream refers to the connection and must be\\n265:   // deleted first.\\n266:   bool reset_stream = false;\\n267:   // If the response encoder is still associated with the stream, reset the stream. The exception\\n268:   // here is when Envoy \\\"ends\\\" the stream by calling recreateStream at which point recreateStream\\n269:   // explicitly nulls out response_encoder to avoid the downstream being notified of the\\n270:   // Envoy-internal stream instance being ended.\\n271:   if (stream.response_encoder_ != nullptr &&\\n272:       (!stream.filter_manager_.hasLastDownstreamByteReceived() ||\\n273:        !stream.state_.codec_saw_local_complete_)) {\\n274:     // Indicate local is complete at this point so that if we reset during a continuation, we don't\\n275:     // raise further data or trailers.\\n276:     ENVOY_STREAM_LOG(debug, \\\"doEndStream() resetting stream\\\", stream);\\n277:     // TODO(snowp): This call might not be necessary, try to clean up + remove setter function.\\n278:     stream.filter_manager_.setLocalComplete();\\n279:     stream.state_.codec_saw_local_complete_ = true;\\n280: \\n281:     // Per https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7540#section-8.3 if there was an error\\n282:     // with the TCP connection during a CONNECT request, it should be\\n283:     // communicated via CONNECT_ERROR\\n284:     if (requestWasConnect(stream.request_headers_, codec_->protocol()) &&\\n285:         (stream.filter_manager_.streamInfo().hasResponseFlag(\\n286:              StreamInfo::CoreResponseFlag::UpstreamConnectionFailure) ||\\n287:          stream.filter_manager_.streamInfo().hasResponseFlag(\\n288:              StreamInfo::CoreResponseFlag::UpstreamConnectionTermination))) {\\n289:       stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::ConnectError);\\n290:     } else {\\n291:       const bool reset_with_error =\\n292:           Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\\\"envoy.reloadable_features.reset_with_error\\\");\\n293:       if (stream.filter_manager_.streamInfo().hasResponseFlag(\\n294:               StreamInfo::CoreResponseFlag::UpstreamProtocolError) &&\\n295:           !Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\\n296:               \\\"envoy.reloadable_features.reset_ignore_upstream_reason\\\")) {\\n297:         stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::ProtocolError);\\n298:       } else if (reset_with_error && stream.filter_manager_.streamInfo().hasResponseFlag(\\n299:                                          StreamInfo::CoreResponseFlag::DownstreamProtocolError)) {\\n300:         stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::ProtocolError);\\n301:       } else {\\n302:         stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::LocalReset);\\n303:       }\\n304:     }\\n305:     reset_stream = true;\\n306:   }\\n307: \\n308:   if (!reset_stream) {\\n309: (check_for_deferred_close) {\\n317:     checkForDeferredClose(stream.shouldSkipDeferredCloseDelay());\\n318:   }\\n319: }\\n320: \\n321: void ConnectionManagerImpl::doDeferredStreamDestroy(ActiveStream& stream) {\\n322:   if (!stream.state_.is_internally_destroyed_) {\\n323:     ++closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_;\\n324:     if \\n259: void ConnectionManagerImpl::doEndStream(ActiveStream& stream, bool check_for_deferred_close) {\\n260:   // The order of what happens in this routine is important and a little complicated. We first see\\n261:   // if the stream needs to be reset. If it needs to be, this will end up invoking reset callbacks\\n262:   // and then moving the stream to the deferred destruction list. If the stream has not been reset,\\n263:   // we move it to the deferred deletion list here. Then, we potentially close the connection. This\\n264:   // must be done after deleting the stream since the stream refers to the connection and must be\\n265:   // deleted first.\\n266:   bool reset_stream = false;\\n267:   // If the response encoder is still associated with the stream, reset the stream. The exception\\n268:   // here is when Envoy \\\"ends\\\" the stream by calling recreateStream at which point recreateStream\\n269:   // explicitly nulls out response_encoder to avoid the downstream being notified of the\\n270:   // Envoy-internal stream instance being ended.\\n271:   if (stream.response_encoder_ != nullptr &&\\n272:       (!stream.filter_manager_.hasLastDownstreamByteReceived() ||\\n273:        !stream.state_.codec_saw_local_complete_)) {\\n274:     // Indicate local is complete at this point so that if we reset during a continuation, we don't\\n275:     // raise further data or trailers.\\n276:     ENVOY_STREAM_LOG(debug, \\\"doEndStream() resetting stream\\\", stream);\\n277:     // TODO(snowp): This call might not be necessary, try to clean up + remove setter function.\\n278:     stream.filter_manager_.setLocalComplete();\\n279:     stream.state_.codec_saw_local_complete_ = true;\\n280: \\n281:     // Per https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7540#section-8.3 if there was an error\\n282:     // with the TCP connection during a CONNECT request, it should be\\n283:     // communicated via CONNECT_ERROR\\n284:     if (requestWasConnect(stream.request_headers_, codec_->protocol()) &&\\n285:         (stream.filter_manager_.streamInfo().hasResponseFlag(\\n286:              StreamInfo::CoreResponseFlag::UpstreamConnectionFailure) ||\\n287:          stream.filter_manager_.streamInfo().hasResponseFlag(\\n288:              StreamInfo::CoreResponseFlag::UpstreamConnectionTermination))) {\\n289:       stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::ConnectError);\\n290:     } else {\\n291:       const bool reset_with_error =\\n292:           Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\\\"envoy.reloadable_features.reset_with_error\\\");\\n293:       if (stream.filter_manager_.streamInfo().hasResponseFlag(\\n294:               StreamInfo::CoreResponseFlag::UpstreamProtocolError) &&\\n295:           !Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\\n296:               \\\"envoy.reloadable_features.reset_ignore_upstream_reason\\\")) {\\n297:         stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::ProtocolError);\\n298:       } else if (reset_with_error && stream.filter_manager_.streamInfo().hasResponseFlag(\\n299:                                          StreamInfo::CoreResponseFlag::DownstreamProtocolError)) {\\n300: {\n260:   // The order of what happens in this routine is important and a little complicated. We first see\n261:   // if the stream needs to be reset. If it needs to be, this will end up invoking reset callbacks\n262:   // and then moving the stream to the deferred destruction list. If the stream has not been reset,\n263:   // we move it to the deferred deletion list here. Then, we potentially close the connection. This\n264:   // must be done after deleting the stream since the stream refers to the connection and must be\n265:   // deleted first.\n266:   bool reset_stream = false;\n267:   // If the response encoder is still associated with the stream, reset the stream. notified of the\n270:   // Envoy-internal stream instance being ended.\n271:   if (stream.response_encoder_ != nullptr &&\n272:       (!stream.filter_manager_.hasLastDownstreamByteReceived() ||\n273: stream.filter_manager_.setLocalComplete();\n279:     stream.state_.codec_saw_local_complete_ = true;\n280: \n281:     // Per https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7540#section-8.3 if there was an error\n282: stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::ConnectError);\n290:     } else {\n291:       const bool reset_with_error =\n292:           Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\"envoy.reloadable_features.reset_with_error\");\n293:       if (stream.filter_manager_.streamInfo().hasResponseFlag(\n294: We want to\n542:     // either redispatch if there are no streams and we have more data. Though we are\n578:     // about to close the connection and will disable further reads, it is possible that flushing\n579:     // data out can cause stream callbacks to fire (e.g., low watermark callbacks).\n580:     //\n581:     // TODO(mattklein123): I tried to actually reset through the codec here, but ran into issues\n582:     // with nghttp2 state and being unhappy about sending reset frames after the connection had\n583:     // been terminated via GOAWAY. }\n599: \n600: void ConnectionManagerImpl::onEvent(Network::ConnectionEvent event) {\n601:   if (event == Network::ConnectionEvent::LocalClose) {\n602: This flag is used to avoid above recursion.\n716:   if (drained_due_to_premature_resets_) {\n717:     return;\n718:   }\n719: \n720:   if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ == 0) {\n721:     return;\n722:   }\n723: \n724:   const uint64_t limit =\n725:       runtime_.snapshot().getInteger(ConnectionManagerImpl::PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey, 500);\n726: \n727:   if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit) {\n728:     // Even though the total number of streams have not reached `limit`, check if the number of bad\n729:     // streams is high enough that even if every subsequent stream is good, the connection\n730:     // would be closed once the limit is reached, and if so close the connection now.\n731:     if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < limit) {\n732:       return;\n733:     }\n734:   } else {\n735:     if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_) {\n736:       return;\n737:     }\n738:   }\n739: \n740:   if (read_callbacks_->connection().state() == Network::Connection::State::Open) {\n741:     stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.inc();\n742: \n743:     // Mark the the connection has been drained due to too many premature resets.\n744:     drained_due_to_premature_resets_ = true;\n745: \n746:     doConnectionClose(Network::ConnectionCloseType::Abort, absl::nullopt,\n747:                       \"too_many_premature_resets\");\n748:   }\n749: }\n750: \n751: void ConnectionManagerImpl::onGoAway(GoAwayErrorCode) {\n752:   // Currently we do nothing with remote go away frames. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_012Rg7kzJK285yd29GUXBxFD","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01GSLR9JXpt4Q38xby6P4GtL","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/coverage_analysis.md","content":"# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager\n\n## Summary\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) in Envoy is the core HTTP processing pipeline responsible for managing connections, routing requests, and executing filter chains. After analyzing the implementation in `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` and its test suite, I identified **5 critical test coverage gaps** that could allow subtle bugs to slip through, particularly around:\n\n1. HTTP/1.0 safe connection duration timeout (soft drain mode)\n2. Deferred request processing with metadata and trailers\n3. Premature reset stream detection and connection draining\n4. CONNECT-UDP request handling and rewriting\n5. Trailer validation protocol-specific behavior\n\nThese gaps represent scenarios that could lead to resource leaks, protocol violations, or incorrect request handling in production.\n\n---\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: HTTP/1.0 Safe Max Connection Duration (Soft Drain Mode)\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: 769-788, 2123-2135\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  When max connection duration is reached on HTTP/1.0, Envoy can enter \"soft drain\" mode instead of immediately draining the connection. In this mode, `soft_drain_http1_` is set to true, and new streams set `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()` flag rather than starting an immediate drain sequence. The `shouldSkipDeferredCloseDelay()` method then uses this flag to decide whether to skip the delayed close timeout.\n\n  The critical untested path is:\n  - HTTP/1.0 connection with max duration timeout configured\n  - `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration()` returns true in config\n  - Connection enters soft drain mode instead of starting drain sequence\n  - New stream created after soft drain is set\n  - Connection should close gracefully after that stream completes\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, HTTP1SafeMaxConnectionDurationSoftDrain)`\n  - **Setup**: Configure HTTP/1.0 codec with `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration() = true` and max connection duration = 100ms\n  - **Execution**:\n    1. Create connection with HTTP/1.0 codec\n    2. Wait for connection duration timeout to trigger\n    3. Verify `drain_state_` is still `NotDraining` (not `Draining`)\n    4. Verify `soft_drain_http1_` flag is set to true\n    5. Create new stream and verify it has `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()` set\n    6. Send response and complete stream\n    7. Verify connection closes after response is sent\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - `stats_.named_.downstream_cx_http1_soft_drain_ == 1`\n    - Connection is closed after stream completes\n    - `drain_state_` transitions from `NotDraining` to `Closing` via stream completion, not via `startDrainSequence()`\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  HTTP/1.0 requires careful handling because it doesn't have explicit framing mechanisms like HTTP/1.1 (which uses chunked encoding) or HTTP/2 (which has frame boundaries). The soft drain mode is designed to ensure graceful shutdown without triggering immediate connection closure, which could violate HTTP/1.0 protocol semantics. Without this test, bugs in soft drain mode could cause:\n  - Premature connection closure breaking in-flight HTTP/1.0 requests\n  - Resource leaks if soft drain flag is set but never cleared\n  - Violation of max connection duration semantics\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Deferred Request Processing with Metadata and Trailers\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: 2533-2604, 1565-1567\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  When `http.max_requests_per_io_cycle` runtime key is set to limit requests processed per I/O cycle, requests exceeding the limit are deferred to the next I/O cycle. The `onDeferredRequestProcessing()` method must replay:\n  1. Request headers\n  2. Any deferred metadata in order\n  3. Request data (if present)\n  4. Request trailers (if present)\n\n  The untested path involves requests with:\n  - Multiple metadata frames interspersed between headers and body\n  - Request data followed by trailers\n  - Correct ordering and end_stream flag computation based on what's deferred\n\n  Specifically, line 2540 computes: `bool end_stream = state_.deferred_end_stream_ && deferred_data_ == nullptr && deferred_request_trailers_ == nullptr && deferred_metadata_.empty();`\n\n  This logic must be tested for all combinations of what's deferred.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, DeferredRequestProcessingWithMetadataAndTrailers)`\n  - **Setup**: Set runtime `http.max_requests_per_io_cycle = 1`; configure filter that stops on first request\n  - **Execution**:\n    1. Send first request with headers-only (will process immediately)\n    2. Complete first request\n    3. Send second request with: headers + metadata_1 + data + metadata_2 + trailers (will defer)\n    4. Verify second request is deferred (not processed in same I/O cycle)\n    5. Trigger deferred request processing\n    6. Verify headers, metadata, data, and trailers are replayed in correct order\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - `requests_during_dispatch_count_ > max_requests_during_dispatch_` causes deferral\n    - On deferred processing: `filter->decode_headers_called_with.headers == expected_headers`\n    - Metadata frames are replayed in order between headers and data\n    - Data is replayed with correct end_stream flag (false because trailers present)\n    - Trailers are replayed last with end_stream = true\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  The deferred request processing mechanism prevents request starvation and allows fair distribution across multiple connections when CPU is saturated. Bugs in metadata/trailer ordering could:\n  - Cause incorrect end-of-stream semantics, hanging requests waiting for trailers that never arrive\n  - Reorder metadata relative to body data, violating HTTP semantics\n  - Lose metadata or trailers entirely if deferred buffer state is not managed correctly\n  - Cause protocol violations in HTTP/2 and HTTP/3 which have explicit metadata semantics\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Premature Reset Stream Detection and Connection Draining\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: 677-749\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  The `isPrematureRstStream()` and `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` methods detect when a stream is reset prematurely (before response is sent) and track the count of such resets. When too many premature resets occur on a single connection, the connection is drained to prevent resource exhaustion attacks.\n\n  The untested paths include:\n  1. **Edge case 1**: Stream lifetime calculation with nanosecond precision (line 681-691)\n     - Must correctly compare current duration against `PrematureResetMinStreamLifetimeSecondsKey` (default 1 second)\n     - Must handle case where duration is exactly at threshold\n\n  2. **Edge case 2**: Response code check (line 697)\n     - Stream without response code is considered premature\n     - Stream with response code is NOT considered premature (even if reset)\n\n  3. **Edge case 3**: Draining decision with recursion protection (line 703-748)\n     - Connection must not drain twice (flag prevents recursion)\n     - Drain only if: `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ >= limit` AND `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 >= closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_`\n     - This ratio-based logic requires specific stream counts to trigger\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, PrematureResetDrainThreshold)`\n  - **Setup**: Set runtime `overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count = 10`, `overload.premature_reset_min_stream_lifetime_seconds = 0`\n  - **Execution**:\n    1. Create 4 streams, let all complete without sending response (all premature)\n    2. Verify `number_premature_stream_resets_ == 4`\n    3. Verify connection is NOT yet drained (4 < 10 total streams needed)\n    4. Create 3 more good streams (with responses)\n    5. Create 3 more premature reset streams\n    6. Now have: 7 total non-internal, 7 premature (7*2 >= 7, and 7 < 10)\n    7. Verify connection is still not drained (need >= 10 total)\n    8. Create 3 more premature resets (10 total closed, 10 premature)\n    9. Verify connection NOW drains (10 >= 10 AND 10*2 >= 10)\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - `drained_due_to_premature_resets_ == false` until threshold reached\n    - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_ == 0` until threshold\n    - Once threshold reached: `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_ == 1`\n    - `doConnectionClose()` called with correct reason\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  This protection mechanism guards against slowloris and similar attacks where clients send requests and reset them before receiving responses, exhausting server resources. Without proper testing:\n  - Premature reset attacks could exhaust server memory/connections\n  - False positives could incorrectly drain legitimate connections\n  - Recursion bug could cause stack overflow during stream destruction\n  - Duration calculation bugs could cause premature resets to be missed\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: CONNECT-UDP Request Authority Rewriting\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: 1444-1450\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  The `decodeHeaders()` method has special handling for CONNECT-UDP requests, which are used for UDP tunneling over HTTP. The code calls `HeaderUtility::rewriteAuthorityForConnectUdp()` to transform the authority header to include the target UDP address:port.\n\n  The untested error path is when this rewriting fails (returns false), which should:\n  1. Send a 404 Not Found response with message \"The path is incorrect for CONNECT-UDP\"\n  2. Set response code details to `ResponseCodeDetails::InvalidPath`\n  3. NOT create a filter chain (early return)\n\n  This is distinct from regular \"missing path\" errors and requires specific handling.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, ConnectUdpInvalidAuthority)`\n  - **Setup**: Configure normal HCM with routing\n  - **Execution**:\n    1. Send CONNECT-UDP request with malformed authority (e.g., missing port, invalid format)\n    2. Mock `HeaderUtility::rewriteAuthorityForConnectUdp()` to return false\n    3. Verify request does NOT reach filter chain (filter creation not called)\n    4. Capture response sent to client\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - Response code == 404 (Not Found)\n    - Response body contains \"The path is incorrect for CONNECT-UDP\"\n    - Response code details == `ResponseCodeDetails::InvalidPath`\n    - Filter chain was NOT created (createFilterChain never called)\n    - No upstream request made\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  CONNECT-UDP is a specialized protocol for UDP tunneling. Improper handling of invalid authority in CONNECT-UDP requests could:\n  - Send incorrect error responses, confusing clients\n  - Attempt to route malformed requests upstream, causing protocol violations\n  - Create filter chains for invalid requests, wasting resources\n  - Obscure the real error reason in logs by using wrong response code details\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: Request Trailer Validation with Protocol-Specific Behavior\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: 1256-1300\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  The `validateTrailers()` method validates request trailers after they're deserialized. Unlike header validation, trailer validation has different behavior per protocol:\n\n  - **HTTP/1.1**: Sends 400 Bad Request on invalid trailers\n  - **HTTP/2**: Resets stream on invalid trailers (NOT sending 400)\n  - **HTTP/3**: Resets stream on invalid trailers (NOT sending 400)\n\n  The untested edge cases are:\n  1. Invalid underscores in trailer headers with HTTP/2/HTTP/3 (should reset, not send 400)\n  2. Invalid trailers with gRPC request (should use gRPC status code in some cases)\n  3. Handling of `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage` flag when false (closes entire connection instead of just stream)\n\n  Specifically, the code at lines 1283-1297 shows:\n  - `InvalidUnderscore` detail triggers reset for H/2\n  - Different handling for H/1 vs H/2+ (sendLocalReply vs reset)\n  - Connection close if `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage` is false\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, InvalidTrailersResetHttp2)`\n  - **Setup**: Set codec protocol to HTTP/2\n  - **Execution**:\n    1. Send request headers and data\n    2. Send response headers from upstream (200 OK)\n    3. Send invalid request trailers (e.g., header with underscore)\n    4. Verify stream is reset, NOT a 400 response sent\n    5. Verify connection stays open (stream-level error, not connection-level)\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - Stream reset called (not encodeHeaders with 400)\n    - Connection NOT closed\n    - No 400 response in wire traffic\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, InvalidTrailersWithStreamErrorFalseClosesConnection)`\n  - **Setup**: Configure `stream_error_on_invalid_http_message = false`\n  - **Execution**:\n    1. Send request headers and data\n    2. Send invalid trailers\n    3. Verify connection close is called (not just stream reset)\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - `connection.close()` called\n    - `handleCodecError()` called with trailer validation error\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Trailers are optional headers sent after the body in HTTP/1.1+. Protocol-specific handling is critical because:\n  - HTTP/2 and HTTP/3 have different framing, requiring stream-level resets instead of HTTP/1.1-style error responses\n  - Sending 400 on HTTP/2 violates protocol (headers already sent)\n  - gRPC uses trailers for error codes and status; incorrect handling breaks gRPC services\n  - Connection closure decisions must respect whether invalid trailers are a stream-level or connection-level error\n\n---\n\n## File References\n\nThe following files were analyzed for this coverage gap assessment:\n\n1. **Primary Implementation**:\n   - Verify connection closes after response is sent\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - `stats_.named_.downstream_cx_http1_soft_drain_ == 1`\n    - Connection is closed after stream completes\n    - `drain_state_` transitions from `NotDraining` to `Closing` via stream completion, not via `startDrainSequence()`\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  HTTP/1.0 requires careful handling because it doesn't have explicit framing mechanisms like HTTP/1.1 (which uses chunked encoding) or HTTP/2 (which has frame boundaries). The soft drain mode is designed to ensure graceful shutdown without triggering immediate connection closure, which could violate HTTP/1.0 protocol semantics. Without this test, bugs in soft drain mode could cause:\n  - Premature connection closure breaking in-flight HTTP/1.0 requests\n  - Resource leaks if soft drain flag is set but never cleared\n  - Violation of max connection duration semantics\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Deferred Request Processing with Metadata and Trailers\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: 2533-2604, 1565-1567\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  When `http.max_requests_per_io_cycle` runtime key is set to limit requests processed per I/O cycle, requests exceeding the limit are deferred to the next I/O cycle. The `onDeferredRequestProcessing()` method must replay:\n  1. Request headers\n  2. Any deferred metadata in order\n  3. Request data (if present)\n  4. Request trailers (if present)\n\n  The untested path involves requests with:\n  - Multiple metadata frames interspersed between headers and body\n  - Request data followed by trailers\n  - Correct ordering and end_stream flag computation based on what's deferred\n\n  Specifically, line 2540 computes: `bool end_stream = state_.deferred_end_stream_ && deferred_data_ == nullptr && deferred_request_trailers_ == nullptr && deferred_metadata_.empty();`\n\n  This logic must be tested for all combinations of what's deferred.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, DeferredRequestProcessingWithMetadataAndTrailers)`\n  - **Setup**: Set runtime `http.max_requests_per_io_cycle = 1`; configure filter that stops on first request\n  - **Execution**:\n    1. Send first request with headers-only (will process immediately)\n    2. Complete first request\n    3. Send second request with: headers + metadata_1 + data + metadata_2 + trailers (will defer)\n    4. Verify second request is deferred (not processed in same I/O cycle)\n    5. Trigger deferred request processing\n    6. Verify headers, metadata, data, and trailers are replayed in correct order\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - `requests_during_dispatch_count_ > max_requests_during_dispatch_` causes deferral\n    - On deferred processing: `filter->decode_headers_called_with.headers == expected_headers`\n    - Metadata frames are replayed in order between headers and data\n    - Data is replayed with correct end_stream flag (false because trailers present)\n    - Trailers are replayed last with end_stream = true\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  The deferred request processing mechanism prevents request starvation and allows fair distribution across multiple connections when CPU is saturated. Bugs in metadata/trailer ordering could:\n  - Cause incorrect end-of-stream semantics, hanging requests waiting for trailers that never arrive\n  - Reorder metadata relative to body data, violating HTTP semantics\n  - Lose metadata or trailers entirely if deferred buffer state is not managed correctly\n  - Cause protocol violations in HTTP/2 and HTTP/3 which have explicit metadata semantics\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Premature Reset Stream Detection and Connection Draining\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: 677-749\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  The `isPrematureRstStream()` and `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` methods detect when a stream is reset prematurely (before response is sent) and track the count of such resets. When too many premature resets occur on a single connection, the connection is drained to prevent resource exhaustion attacks.\n\n  The untested paths include:\n  1. **Edge case 1**: Stream lifetime calculation with nanosecond precision (line 681-691)\n     - Must correctly compare current duration against `PrematureResetMinStreamLifetimeSecondsKey` (default 1 second)\n     - Must handle case where duration is exactly at threshold\n\n  2. **Edge case 2**: Response code check (line 697)\n     - Stream without response code is considered premature\n     - Stream with response code is NOT considered premature (even if reset)\n\n  3. **Edge case 3**: Draining decision with recursion protection (line 703-748)\n     - Connection must not drain twice (flag prevents recursion)\n     - Drain only if: `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ >= limit` AND `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 >= closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_`\n     - This ratio-based logic requires specific stream counts to trigger\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, PrematureResetDrainThreshold)`\n  - **Setup**: Set runtime `overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count = 10`, `overload.premature_reset_min_stream_lifetime_seconds = 0`\n  - **Execution**:\n    1. Create 4 streams, let all complete without sending response (all premature)\n    2. Verify `number_premature_stream_resets_ == 4`\n    3. Verify connection is NOT yet drained (4 < 10 total streams needed)\n    4. Create 3 more good streams (with responses)\n    5. Create 3 more premature reset streams\n    6. Now have: 7 total non-internal, 7 premature (7*2 >= 7, and 7 < 10)\n    7. Verify connection is still not drained (need >= 10 total)\n    8. Create 3 more premature resets (10 total closed, 10 premature)\n    9. Verify connection NOW drains (10 >= 10 AND 10*2 >= 10)\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - `drained_due_to_premature_resets_ == false` until threshold reached\n    - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_ == 0` until threshold\n    - Once threshold reached: `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_ == 1`\n    - `doConnectionClose()` called with correct reason\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  This protection mechanism guards against slowloris and similar attacks where clients send requests and reset them before receiving responses, exhausting server resources. Without proper testing:\n  - Premature reset attacks could exhaust server memory/connections\n  - False positives could incorrectly drain legitimate connections\n  - Recursion bug could cause stack overflow during stream destruction\n  - Duration calculation bugs could cause premature resets to be missed\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: CONNECT-UDP Request Authority Rewriting\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: 1444-1450\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  The `decodeHeaders()` method has special handling for CONNECT-UDP requests, which are used for UDP tunneling over HTTP. The code calls `HeaderUtility::rewriteAuthorityForConnectUdp()` to transform the authority header to include the target UDP address:port.\n\n  The untested error path is when this rewriting fails (returns false), which should:\n  1. Send a 404 Not Found response with message \"The path is incorrect for CONNECT-UDP\"\n  2. Set response code details to `ResponseCodeDetails::InvalidPath`\n  3. NOT create a filter chain (early return)\n\n  This is distinct from regular \"missing path\" errors and requires specific handling.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, ConnectUdpInvalidAuthority)`\n  - **Setup**: Configure normal HCM with routing\n  - **Execution**:\n    1. Send CONNECT-UDP request with malformed authority (e.g., missing port, invalid format)\n    2. Mock `HeaderUtility::rewriteAuthorityForConnectUdp()` to return false\n    3. Verify request does NOT reach filter chain (filter creation not called)\n    4. Capture response sent to client\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - Response code == 404 (Not Found)\n    - Response body contains \"The path is incorrect for CONNECT-UDP\"\n    - Response code details == `ResponseCodeDetails::InvalidPath`\n    - Filter chain was NOT created (createFilterChain never called)\n    - No upstream request made\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  CONNECT-UDP is a specialized protocol for UDP tunneling. Improper handling of invalid authority in CONNECT-UDP requests could:\n  - Send incorrect error responses, confusing clients\n  - Attempt to route malformed requests upstream, causing protocol violations\n  - Create filter chains for invalid requests, wasting resources\n  - Obscure the real error reason in logs by using wrong response code details\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: Request Trailer Validation with Protocol-Specific Behavior\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: 1256-1300\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  The `validateTrailers()` method validates request trailers after they're deserialized. Unlike header validation, trailer validation has different behavior per protocol:\n\n  - **HTTP/1.1**: Sends 400 Bad Request on invalid trailers\n  - **HTTP/2**: Resets stream on invalid trailers (NOT sending 400)\n  - **HTTP/3**: Resets stream on invalid trailers (NOT sending 400)\n\n  The untested edge cases are:\n  1. Invalid underscores in trailer headers with HTTP/2/HTTP/3 (should reset, not send 400)\n  2. Invalid trailers with gRPC request (should use gRPC status code in some cases)\n  3. Handling of `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage` flag when false (closes entire connection instead of just stream)\n\n  Specifically, the code at lines 1283-1297 shows:\n  - `InvalidUnderscore` detail triggers reset for H/2\n  - Different handling for H/1 vs H/2+ (sendLocalReply vs reset)\n  - Connection close if `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage` is false\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, InvalidTrailersResetHttp2)`\n  - **Setup**: Set codec protocol to HTTP/2\n  - **Execution**:\n    1. Send request headers and data\n    2. Send response headers from upstream (200 OK)\n    3. Send invalid request trailers (e.g., header with underscore)\n    4. Verify stream is reset, NOT a 400 response sent\n    5. Verify connection stays open (stream-level error, not connection-level)\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - Stream reset called (not encodeHeaders with 400)\n    - Connection NOT closed\n    - No 400 response in wire traffic\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, InvalidTrailersWithStreamErrorFalseClosesConnection)`\n  - **Setup**: Configure `stream_error_on_invalid_http_message = false`\n  - **Execution**:\n    1. Send request headers and data\n    2. Send invalid trailers\n    3. Verify connection close is called (not just stream reset)\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - `connection.close()` called\n    - `handleCodecError()` called with trailer validation error\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Trailers are optional headers sent after the body in HTTP/1.1+. Protocol-specific handling is critical because:\n  - HTTP/2 and HTTP/3 have different framing, requiring stream-level resets instead of HTTP/1.1-style error responses\n  - Sending 400 on HTTP/2 violates protocol (headers already sent)\n  - gRPC uses trailers for error codes and status; incorrect handling breaks gRPC services\n  - Connection closure decisions must respect whether invalid trailers are a stream-level or connection-level error\n\n---\n\n## File References\n\nThe following files were analyzed for this coverage gap assessment:\n\n1. **Primary Implementation**:\n   -
